			- Day 4
			  collapsed:: true
				- Authentication and Authorisation
				  id:: 646349f5-850a-4bf6-ace6-ab463763e0ec
					- 1) Intro to Authentication and Authorisation
					  id:: 646349f5-99e6-49a5-9e82-fa0b79023382
						- First task
							- **Resources**
								- [What is Authentication](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tZPENgB_Rd0)
								  id:: 646349f5-7576-44b1-8f40-8e1b3fb3efed
									- Authentication is the act of identifying a user or a device.
									- Verifying the identity of the specific user ("Are you who you say you are?")
									- Triggered once per session
									- Examples
										- Something you know e.g. password
										- Something you have e.g. OTP
										- Something you are e.g. biometric
								- [What is Authorisation](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gnZo3BJgjpI)
									- Authorization ts the act of allowing or denying users and devices access rights.
									- Deciding whether a user is allowed to do something ("Do you have permission?")
									- Checks whether the value given is what is expected
									- Then checks what roles the user has, thus what permissions it has access to
								- *Comparisons*
									- [Authentication vs Authorisation explained](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2iTTBJd46ow)
										- Triggered per-request/operation
										- "I know you, but do I trust you?"
										- Examples
											- Passport = authentication
											- Boarding pass = authorisation
										- Authorisation depends on Authentication
									- [Authorization vs Authentication - Whats the Difference? | Developer Concepts Explained - YouTube](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=85BBfKo6bdo)
							- **Questions to answer**
								- What is authentication?
								- What is authorisation?
								- When might you want to add authentication/authorisation to your app? When might you not want to?
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1669892347138_0.png)
						- Fundamental security measures
							- Hashing and Salting
								- e.g. ((63888994-6553-4a68-97ab-ffd052af43f6))
							- Encryption
						- Providers
							- ![image.png](../assets/image_1669892610159_0.png)
						- Today we're going to use Auth0
							- ![image.png](../assets/image_1669892649763_0.png)
					- 2) Using Authentication Services vs Building Your Own
						- Second task
						  collapsed:: true
							- **Resources**
								- [Please everyone, stop writing your own user authentication code | With Blue Ink](https://withblue.ink/2020/04/08/stop-writing-your-own-user-authentication-code.html)
								- [Should you Implement Authentication Yourself? - YouTube](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Hh_kiZTTBr0)
									- Pros/Cons of rolling your own authentication (using FOSS libraries)
										- Pros
											- Maybe more secure than FOSS libraries like passport.js
											- Their servers are likely more secure
										- Cons
											- Slower to setup
											- Frontend developers don't have to learn this backend tech
											- Big Tech gets control of your user data
											- Costs money
									- FOSS alternatives
									  id:: 63974fae-ea36-4574-b068-7eba4a7e8918
										- Related: ((63a3166e-79ac-429a-b496-f58e487b3016))
								- [https://auth0.com/blog/5-massive-benefits-of-identity-as-a-service-for-developers/](https://auth0.com/blog/5-massive-benefits-of-identity-as-a-service-for-developers/)
								- Watch the first 100s of this one (you can ignore the stuff after 100s, as it's not directly relevant)**: **[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yufqeJLP1rI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yufqeJLP1rI)
							- **Questions to answer**
								- What are the pros/cons of implementing a signup/login system yourself?
								- What are the pros/cons of using a 3rd party service to manage it for you?

			- Day 1
			  collapsed:: true
				- Talk with Trenton Moss (from Team Sterka)
				  collapsed:: true
					- Treat other people the way they want to be treated, NOT "treat people the way you want to be wanted"
					- [Personality Test](https://sterka.team/comms-style) - My comms style is: **Director**
					  collapsed:: true
						- You are: Director - 35%, Thinker - 28%, Socialiser - 21%, Relater - 16%
							- ![image.png](../assets/image_1670237078442_0.png)
							- Now  = Optimise the now
								- Cons
									- Could be called slow, cautious
							- Future = Focus on the future
								- Cons
									- Could be accused of being a bit too fast, risk-taker
						- Director
							- Unsure
								- You don't show emotion a lot of the time
								- Impatient because others can't see the "obvious" answers infront of you
								- Obsessed with control
								- Decisive
						-
					- How to talk with different personality types
					  collapsed:: true
						- Meeting a Relater
							- Be non-threatening and truly sincere
							- Have a slow and reassuring manner
							- Constantly show that you're listening
							- Share personal opinions and feelings (don’t push facts/logic)
							- Allow time to solicit opinions from others
							- Be interested in them as a person and their emotions
						- Meeting a Director
							- Meetings are shorter, but you need to spend more time to prepare
							- Be super-efficient and competent
							- Let them take control - offer options, not solutions
							- Keep it high-level and straight-to-the-point
							- Be very well prepared so you're able to answer questions
							- Don't waste their time (no need for personal chat)
							- Use facts/data to backup your arguments (never feelings!)
							- Recognise their ideas and ability to achieve results
						- Meeting a Thinker
							- Be thorough, well-prepared and patient
							- Don't rush them into decision-making
							- State pros and cons, with ways to overcome the cons
							- Provide clear evidence of your solutions (and confirm in writing)
							- Gather lots of data to support your arguments
							- Don't waste time with small talk
							- Compliment them on their brain power and efficiency
						- Meeting a Socialiser
							- Be very interested in them and give compliments
							- Recognise and get excited by their ideas
							- Talk mostly about the big picture impact
							- Don't rush into getting down to business
							- Be very direct about your expectations of them in writing
							- Use storytelling to put forward your ideas
							- Help them to look good in front of others
					- How to find out what comm style people is
						- 1) Ask "How are you?"
							- Director: "Yeah I'm fine, let's get on with the meeting"
							- Socialiser: excited and will tell you what they were up to
							- Relater: they'll ask you back how are you
							- Thinker: Very little response

			- Day 4
			  collapsed:: true
				- Couchbase talk 2
				  id:: 63904f45-75cb-44d9-a073-f86950b882f5
				  collapsed:: true
					- Intro
						- [Kahoot!](https://kahoot.it/) being used for real-time group multiple-choice quiz
						- Key-value databases can be manipulated through CRUD, but document types can't
						- NoSQL databases can be scaled horizontally, SQL databases not (MySQL replication doesn't count?)
						- Key-value is most commonly used for caching
					- Data structure
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1670508229897_0.png)
					- The underlying document is JSON, but the syntax used is nearly identical to SQL (they call it SQL++)
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1670508358890_0.png)
					- Deployment options
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1670508563310_0.png)
					- Some useful snippets for Node.js API
					  collapsed:: true
						- ```javascript
						  Upsert to create or update...
						  
						  // Upsert a document when concurrent writes are OK or when you
						  // are ingesting bulk data.
						  const upsertResult = await hotelCollection.upsert('hotel-123', document)
						  
						  // Each document modification changes the CAS value.
						  console.log('CAS:', upsertResult.cas);
						  
						  
						  // Do big things with just a few lines...
						  
						  // Quickly solve complex data access challenges.
						  const getRoutesFromCity = async (CITY) => {
						    const query = `
						      SELECT *
						      FROM sample.inventory.airport a
						      INNER NEST sample.inventory.route r
						      ON a.faa = r.sourceairport
						      WHERE a.city = $CITY
						      ORDER BY a.airportname;`;
						  
						    // Named parameters allow flexibility and dynamic queries
						    const options = {
						      parameters: {
						        CITY,
						      },
						    };
						    return await database.query(query, options);
						  }
						  
						  //Be faster and more precise...
						  
						  // Sometimes you do not want to work with an entire document.
						  // To change a specific field inside a document, you can perform
						  // Sub-Document operations!
						  
						  // Quickly update just one document field...
						  await hotelCollection.mutateIn('hotel-123', [
						    couchbase.MutateInSpec.upsert('pets_ok', true),
						  ])
						  
						  // Increment or decrement sub-document counters...
						  await collection.mutateIn('customer123', [
						    couchbase.MutateInSpec.increment('logins', 1),
						  ])
						  
						  // Easily work with sub-document arrays...
						  await collection.mutateIn('customer123', [
						    couchbase.MutateInSpec.arrayInsert('tags[0]', 'easier'),
						  ])
						  
						  //Find documents fast...
						  
						  // Use full-text search to help your users quickly
						  // find the documents they are looking for..
						  async function ftsMatchPhrase(phrase) {
						    return await cluster.searchQuery(
						      'index-hotel-description',
						      couchbase.SearchQuery.matchPhrase(phrase),
						      { limit: 10 }
						    )
						  }
						  
						  await ftsMatchPhrase('10-minute walk from the')
						  
						  // Bring your solutions to the edge...
						  
						  // Take your data to the edge with App Services. In this example,
						  // our changes will be replicated to Capella when the mobile phone
						  // comes back online.
						  let database = try!Database(name: "hoteldb");
						  
						  // Create a document with the Swift SDK.
						  var mutableDoc = MutableDocument(id: "doc1");
						  
						  // Mutate the document.
						  mutableDoc.setFloat(121.75, forKey:"room_rate");
						  
						  // Save the document.
						  try!database.saveDocument(mutableDoc);
						  
						  
						  // Easily create a document...
						  
						  // Insert the document in the hotel collection.
						  const insertResult = await hotelCollection.insert('hotel-123', document);
						  
						  console.log('CAS:', insertResult.cas);
						  ```
					- After having setup a free cluster on AWS via [Couchbase Capella](https://cloud.couchbase.com)
						- Yes 30 free days with Capella ( the fully hosted managed solution). You can get community version (Couchbase Server) for free
						- `Cluster > Settings > Buckets` = where you can control the data that's in your cluster
						- `Cluster > Data Tools > Documents` = see sample data
							- JSON for the document data + metadata
					- How to access your data
						- Queries using Key/Value - manipulated through CRUD operations
						- Query using SQL++
						- Full Text Search
					- ![image.png](../assets/image_1670512400516_0.png)
					- Cons of SQL
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1670512535555_0.png)
					- SQL++
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1670512687374_0.png)
						- m unsure about other document databases but within Couchbase SQL++ is usually the primary way of querying the data, along with Full Text Search, which we’re going to talk about next
					- ![Lab 1 Querying in Couchbase using SQL++.pdf](../assets/Lab_1_Querying_in_Couchbase_using_SQL++_1670512960709_0.pdf)
						- ```sql
						  SELECT state, city
						  FROM `travel-sample`.inventory-hotel
						  WHERE state = 'California';
						  ```
						- `SELECT * FROM `travel-sample`.inventory.hotel WHERE country="France"`

			- Day 5 - Hackathon Fridays
			  collapsed:: true
				- `useFetch` ((63909c79-1a45-4724-9f97-086c3c278e32))
				  id:: 63949785-b051-42e5-b85e-38551cea11a8
				  collapsed:: true
					- `/src/hooks/useFetch.js`
					  ```javascript
					  import { useState, useEffect } from "react";
					  
					  export default function useFetch(url) {
					    const [person, setBootcamper] = useState("");
					    const [error, setError] = useState(null);
					  
					    useEffect(() => {
					      async function fetchStuff() {
					        try {
					          const responseJSON = await fetch(url);
					          const result = await responseJSON.json();
					          setBootcamper(result);
					        } catch (e) {
					          setError(e);
					        }
					      }
					      fetchStuff();
					    }, [url]);
					    return { person, error };
					  }
					  ```
						- ((63f8fe5a-255e-4682-b228-cc2790a41d73)):
							- This is a custom `useFetch` hook that makes it easy to fetch data from a given URL and store the result in the `person` state variable. It also keeps track of any errors that may occur in a separate `error` state variable.
							- The `useFetch` hook uses the `useState` and `useEffect` hooks from the `react` library to manage its internal state and handle fetching data from the specified URL.
							- When the `useFetch` hook is called, it returns an object with two properties: `person` and `error`. The `person` property contains the data that was fetched from the URL, and the `error` property contains any error that may have occurred during the fetch operation.
							- The `useFetch` hook is designed to be used in a React functional component. When the component is rendered, the `useFetch` hook will fetch the data from the specified URL and update the component's state with the result. The component can then use this data to render the fetched content.
					- Related: ((639cb088-a174-4266-9211-52b82a1772f0))

				- TypeScript intro
				  id:: 63974fae-4583-480d-9c40-d4ed17c273ee
					- Intro learning
						- To begin with, watch these videos:
							- [TypeScript in 100 Seconds - YouTube](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zQnBQ4tB3ZA)
							  collapsed:: true
								- {{video https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zQnBQ4tB3ZA}}
									- If you initialise a variable with a value, it'll **infer** the type, however you can explicitly make the type `any` if you intend for it to change types later
										- ```typescript
										  let variable1 = 'hello';
										  variable1 = 23; // this will show an error
										  
										  let variable2: any = 'hello';
										  variable1 = 23; // this will work
										  ```
							- [TypeScript - The Basics - YouTube](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ahCwqrYpIuM)
							  collapsed:: true
								- {{video https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ahCwqrYpIuM}}
								- TypeScript Deep Dive book by Basarat Ali Syed
								- Steps
									- `tsc index.ts`
									- `touch tsconfig.json` = create a tsconfig file. See docs for all the options available
									  collapsed:: true
										- SoC recommended (with minimal code comments)
											- ```json
											  {
											    "compilerOptions": {
											      /* Language and Environment */
											      "target": "es2016",
											      /* Modules */
											      "module": "ES6",         /* Specify what module code is generated. */
											      "rootDir": "./src",        /* Specify the root folder within your source files. */
											      /* Emit */
											      "outDir": "./build",        /* Specify an output folder for all emitted files. */
											      "noEmitOnError": true,        /* Disable emitting files if any type checking errors are reported. */
											  	/* Interop Constraints */
											      "esModuleInterop": true,       /* Emit additional JavaScript to ease support for importing CommonJS modules. This enables 'allowSyntheticDefaultImports' for type compatibility. */
											      "forceConsistentCasingInFileNames": true,     /* Ensure that casing is correct in imports. */
											      /* Type Checking */
											      "strict": true,         /* Enable all strict type-checking options. */
											      /* Completeness */
											      "skipLibCheck": true    /* Skip type checking all .d.ts files. */
											    }
											  }
											  ```
										- SoC recommended (with full code comments)

											- ```json
											  {
											    "compilerOptions": {
											      /* Visit [TypeScript: TSConfig Reference - Docs on every TSConfig option](https://aka.ms/tsconfig) to read more about this file */
											  
											      /* Projects */
											      // "incremental": true,                              /* Save .tsbuildinfo files to allow for incremental compilation of projects. */
											      // "composite": true,                                /* Enable constraints that allow a TypeScript project to be used with project references. */
											      // "tsBuildInfoFile": "./.tsbuildinfo",              /* Specify the path to .tsbuildinfo incremental compilation file. */
											      // "disableSourceOfProjectReferenceRedirect": true,  /* Disable preferring source files instead of declaration files when referencing composite projects. */
											      // "disableSolutionSearching": true,                 /* Opt a project out of multi-project reference checking when editing. */
											      // "disableReferencedProjectLoad": true,             /* Reduce the number of projects loaded automatically by TypeScript. */
											  
											      /* Language and Environment */
											      "target": "es2016",                                  /* Set the JavaScript language version for emitted JavaScript and include compatible library declarations. */
											      // "lib": [],                                        /* Specify a set of bundled library declaration files that describe the target runtime environment. */
											      // "jsx": "preserve",                                /* Specify what JSX code is generated. */
											      // "experimentalDecorators": true,                   /* Enable experimental support for TC39 stage 2 draft decorators. */
											      // "emitDecoratorMetadata": true,                    /* Emit design-type metadata for decorated declarations in source files. */
											      // "jsxFactory": "",                                 /* Specify the JSX factory function used when targeting React JSX emit, e.g. 'React.createElement' or 'h'. */
											      // "jsxFragmentFactory": "",                         /* Specify the JSX Fragment reference used for fragments when targeting React JSX emit e.g. 'React.Fragment' or 'Fragment'. */
											      // "jsxImportSource": "",                            /* Specify module specifier used to import the JSX factory functions when using 'jsx: react-jsx*'. */
											      // "reactNamespace": "",                             /* Specify the object invoked for 'createElement'. This only applies when targeting 'react' JSX emit. */
											      // "noLib": true,                                    /* Disable including any library files, including the default lib.d.ts. */
											      // "useDefineForClassFields": true,                  /* Emit ECMAScript-standard-compliant class fields. */
											      // "moduleDetection": "auto",                        /* Control what method is used to detect module-format JS files. */
											  
											      /* Modules */
											      "module": "ES6",                                /* Specify what module code is generated. */
											      "rootDir": "./src",                                  /* Specify the root folder within your source files. */
											      // "moduleResolution": "node",                       /* Specify how TypeScript looks up a file from a given module specifier. */
											      // "baseUrl": "./",                                  /* Specify the base directory to resolve non-relative module names. */
											      // "paths": {},                                      /* Specify a set of entries that re-map imports to additional lookup locations. */
											      // "rootDirs": [],                                   /* Allow multiple folders to be treated as one when resolving modules. */
											      // "typeRoots": [],                                  /* Specify multiple folders that act like './node_modules/@types'. */
											      // "types": [],                                      /* Specify type package names to be included without being referenced in a source file. */
											      // "allowUmdGlobalAccess": true,                     /* Allow accessing UMD globals from modules. */
											      // "moduleSuffixes": [],                             /* List of file name suffixes to search when resolving a module. */
											      // "resolveJsonModule": true,                        /* Enable importing .json files. */
											      // "noResolve": true,                                /* Disallow 'import's, 'require's or '<reference>'s from expanding the number of files TypeScript should add to a project. */
											  
											      /* JavaScript Support */
											      // "allowJs": true,                                  /* Allow JavaScript files to be a part of your program. Use the 'checkJS' option to get errors from these files. */
											      // "checkJs": true,                                  /* Enable error reporting in type-checked JavaScript files. */
											      // "maxNodeModuleJsDepth": 1,                        /* Specify the maximum folder depth used for checking JavaScript files from 'node_modules'. Only applicable with 'allowJs'. */
											  
											      /* Emit */
											      // "declaration": true,                              /* Generate .d.ts files from TypeScript and JavaScript files in your project. */
											      // "declarationMap": true,                           /* Create sourcemaps for d.ts files. */
											      // "emitDeclarationOnly": true,                      /* Only output d.ts files and not JavaScript files. */
											      // "sourceMap": true,                                /* Create source map files for emitted JavaScript files. */
											      // "outFile": "./",                                  /* Specify a file that bundles all outputs into one JavaScript file. If 'declaration' is true, also designates a file that bundles all .d.ts output. */
											      "outDir": "./build",                                   /* Specify an output folder for all emitted files. */
											      // "removeComments": true,                           /* Disable emitting comments. */
											      // "noEmit": true,                                   /* Disable emitting files from a compilation. */
											      // "importHelpers": true,                            /* Allow importing helper functions from tslib once per project, instead of including them per-file. */
											      // "importsNotUsedAsValues": "remove",               /* Specify emit/checking behavior for imports that are only used for types. */
											      // "downlevelIteration": true,                       /* Emit more compliant, but verbose and less performant JavaScript for iteration. */
											      // "sourceRoot": "",                                 /* Specify the root path for debuggers to find the reference source code. */
											      // "mapRoot": "",                                    /* Specify the location where debugger should locate map files instead of generated locations. */
											      // "inlineSourceMap": true,                          /* Include sourcemap files inside the emitted JavaScript. */
											      // "inlineSources": true,                            /* Include source code in the sourcemaps inside the emitted JavaScript. */
											      // "emitBOM": true,                                  /* Emit a UTF-8 Byte Order Mark (BOM) in the beginning of output files. */
											      // "newLine": "crlf",                                /* Set the newline character for emitting files. */
											      // "stripInternal": true,                            /* Disable emitting declarations that have '@internal' in their JSDoc comments. */
											      // "noEmitHelpers": true,                            /* Disable generating custom helper functions like '__extends' in compiled output. */
											      "noEmitOnError": true,                            /* Disable emitting files if any type checking errors are reported. */
											      // "preserveConstEnums": true,                       /* Disable erasing 'const enum' declarations in generated code. */
											      // "declarationDir": "./",                           /* Specify the output directory for generated declaration files. */
											      // "preserveValueImports": true,                     /* Preserve unused imported values in the JavaScript output that would otherwise be removed. */
											  
											      /* Interop Constraints */
											      // "isolatedModules": true,                          /* Ensure that each file can be safely transpiled without relying on other imports. */
											      // "allowSyntheticDefaultImports": true,             /* Allow 'import x from y' when a module doesn't have a default export. */
											      "esModuleInterop": true,                             /* Emit additional JavaScript to ease support for importing CommonJS modules. This enables 'allowSyntheticDefaultImports' for type compatibility. */
											      // "preserveSymlinks": true,                         /* Disable resolving symlinks to their realpath. This correlates to the same flag in node. */
											      "forceConsistentCasingInFileNames": true,            /* Ensure that casing is correct in imports. */
											  
											      /* Type Checking */
											      "strict": true,                                      /* Enable all strict type-checking options. */
											      // "noImplicitAny": true,                            /* Enable error reporting for expressions and declarations with an implied 'any' type. */
											      // "strictNullChecks": true,                         /* When type checking, take into account 'null' and 'undefined'. */
											      // "strictFunctionTypes": true,                      /* When assigning functions, check to ensure parameters and the return values are subtype-compatible. */
											      // "strictBindCallApply": true,                      /* Check that the arguments for 'bind', 'call', and 'apply' methods match the original function. */
											      // "strictPropertyInitialization": true,             /* Check for class properties that are declared but not set in the constructor. */
											      // "noImplicitThis": true,                           /* Enable error reporting when 'this' is given the type 'any'. */
											      // "useUnknownInCatchVariables": true,               /* Default catch clause variables as 'unknown' instead of 'any'. */
											      // "alwaysStrict": true,                             /* Ensure 'use strict' is always emitted. */
											      // "noUnusedLocals": true,                           /* Enable error reporting when local variables aren't read. */
											      // "noUnusedParameters": true,                       /* Raise an error when a function parameter isn't read. */
											      // "exactOptionalPropertyTypes": true,               /* Interpret optional property types as written, rather than adding 'undefined'. */
											      // "noImplicitReturns": true,                        /* Enable error reporting for codepaths that do not explicitly return in a function. */
											      // "noFallthroughCasesInSwitch": true,               /* Enable error reporting for fallthrough cases in switch statements. */
											      // "noUncheckedIndexedAccess": true,                 /* Add 'undefined' to a type when accessed using an index. */
											      // "noImplicitOverride": true,                       /* Ensure overriding members in derived classes are marked with an override modifier. */
											      // "noPropertyAccessFromIndexSignature": true,       /* Enforces using indexed accessors for keys declared using an indexed type. */
											      // "allowUnusedLabels": true,                        /* Disable error reporting for unused labels. */
											      // "allowUnreachableCode": true,                     /* Disable error reporting for unreachable code. */
											  
											      /* Completeness */
											      // "skipDefaultLibCheck": true,                      /* Skip type checking .d.ts files that are included with TypeScript. */
											      "skipLibCheck": true                                 /* Skip type checking all .d.ts files. */
											    }
											  }

										- `create-react-app` defaults
											- ```json
											  {
											    "compilerOptions": {
											      "target": "es5",
											      "lib": [
											        "dom",
											        "dom.iterable",
											        "esnext"
											      ],
											      "allowJs": true,
											      "skipLibCheck": true,
											      "esModuleInterop": true,
											      "allowSyntheticDefaultImports": true,
											      "strict": true,
											      "forceConsistentCasingInFileNames": true,
											      "noFallthroughCasesInSwitch": true,
											      "module": "esnext",
											      "moduleResolution": "node",
											      "resolveJsonModule": true,
											      "isolatedModules": true,
											      "noEmit": true,
											      "jsx": "react-jsx"
											    },
											    "include": [
											      "src"
											    ]
											  }
											  
											  ```
										- From a YouTube tutorial
											- ```json
											  "compilerOptions": { 
											    "target": "es3", 
											    "watch": true,
											    "lib": ["dom", "es2017"]
											  }
											  ```
								- Example 3rd-party library importing
									- `npm i lodash`
									- `npm i -D @types/lodash`
								- How to define a basic variable (primitive)
								  ```typescript
								  let varible1: any = 23; 
								  
								  let variable2 = 23; // do this only if you want to have TS infer the type as `number`
								  
								  let boolean1: boolean = true;
								  
								  let hello: string = 'world';
								  
								  let weight: number = 23;
								  ```
								- How to declare arrays containing one type
								  ```typescript
								  let array1: boolean[] = [true, false, true];
								  
								  let array2: number[] = [1, 2, 3];
								  
								  let arra3: string[] = ['a', 'b', 'c']
								  ```
								- You can use `type` or `interface` to define what value and type you're expecting a variable to have:
								  ```typescript
								  type Style = 'bold' | ‘italic’ | 23; 
								  let font: Style;
								  font = ‘something’
								  ```
								- Objects
									- ```typescript
									  interface Describe {
									    amount: number; 
									    uniqueld: string; 
									    isValid: boolean; 
									    addressLines: string[];
									  }
									  
									  let something : Describe = { 
									    amount: 7,
									    uniqueId: "hello",
									    isValid: true,
									    addressLines: ["hello", "bye"]
									  }
									  ```
									- You can use `[key: string]: any` for example in order to create an object that will accept any type of property
									  ```typescript
									  interface Person {
									    first: string;
									    middle: string;
									    last: string;
									    [key: string]: any
									  }
									  
									  const person: Person = {
									    first: 'Jeff',
									    middle: 'Bill',
									    last: 'Delaney'
									  }
									  
									  const person2: Person = {
									    first: 'Usain',
									    middle: 'Something',
									    last: 'Bolt',
									    fast: true
									  }
									  ```
								- Functions
									- ```typescript
									  function pow(x: number, y: number) : number {
									    Math.pow(x, y).toString();
									  }
									  
									  pow(5, 10)
									  ```
									- Tuples
										- ```typescript
										  type MyList = [number?, string?, boolean?];
										  
										  const arr: MyList = []
										  
										  arr.push(1)
										  arr.push('23')
										  arr.push(false)
										  ```
											- Tuples are like arrays which can expect a different type for each item
											- Can also use optional chaining `?` also to make some or all of these optional
									- Use `void` if you are not using the keyword `return` e.g. your function just pushes to an array. Otherwise use the type that you're expecting e.g. `string`, `number`
									  ```typescript
									  function pow(x: number, y: number) : void {
									    Math.pow(x, y).toString();
									  }
									  
									  pow(5, 10)
									  ```
								- Generics
									- They're a way to define the subtype of a type?
									- Examples
										- ```typescript
										  class Observable<T> { 
										    constructor(public value: T) {}
										  } 
										  
										  let x: Observable<number>; 
										  
										  let y: Observable<Person>;
										  
										  let z = new Observable(23)
										  ```
										- ```typescript
										  router.get('/students', async function(req:Request, res:Response):Promise<void> {
										      const result = await getWizardByName(req.query.name);
										      res.status(200).json({ success: true, payload: result });
										  })
										  
										  export async function getWizardByName(name):Promise<void> {
										      const bootcamper = await query(`SELECT name, about FROM bootcampers WHERE name ILIKE $1 ;`,['%'+ name + '%']);
										      return bootcamper.rows;
										  }
										  
										  async function fetchKanyeQuote(): Promise<Quote>{
										    const response = await fetch(`https://api.kanye.rest`);
										    const result:Quote = await response.json();
										    return result;
										  };
										  ```
								- Enums
									- Pros/Cons
										- Pros
											- Much nicer than using union types with string literals, or multiple consts
											  collapsed:: true
												- Enums version
												  ```typescript
												  enum Choice { ROCK, PAPER, SCISSORS }
												  
												  type PlayerMove = Choice | null;
												  
												  export function getRandomComputerMove() : Choice {
												    const choice = Math.trunc(Math.random() * 3);
												    switch (choice) {
												      case 0:
												        return Choice.ROCK;
												      case 1:
												        return Choice.PAPER;
												      case 2:
												        return Choice.SCISSORS;
												      default:
												        throw new Error(`Unsupported choice: ${choice}`);
												    }
												  }
												  ```
												- Multiple consts version
												  ```typescript
												  export const CHOICE_ROCK = "ROCK";
												  export const CHOICE_PAPER = "PAPER";
												  export const CHOICE_SCISSORS = "SCISSORS";
												  
												  type PlayerMove = 'ROCK' | 'PAPER' | 'SCISSORS' | null;
												  
												  export function getRandomComputerMove(): CHOICE_ROCK | CHOICE_PAPER | CHOICE_SCISSORS {
												    const choice = Math.trunc(Math.random() * 3);
												    switch (choice) {
												      case 0:
												        return CHOICE_ROCK;
												      case 1:
												        return CHOICE_PAPER;
												      case 2:
												        return CHOICE_SCISSORS;
												      default:
												        throw new Error(`Unsupported choice: ${choice}`);
												    }
												  }
												  ```
												- Union types with string literals e.g.
												  ```javascript
												  type Choice = 'ROCK' | 'PAPER' | 'SCISSORS';
												  
												  export function getRandomComputerMove(): Choice {
												    const choice = Math.trunc(Math.random() * 3);
												    switch (choice) {
												      case 0:
												        return 'ROCK';
												      case 1:
												        return 'PAPER';
												      case 2:
												        return 'SCISSORS';
												      default:
												        throw new Error(`Unsupported choice: ${choice}`);
												    }
												  }
												  ```
										- Cons
											- [Not recommended by Theo](https://youtu.be/Anu8vHXsavo) because they are falsy. Instead recommends string literals or an array of consts
											- Not recommended by another post I saw because it can't compile to valid JavaScript
									- Example 1
									  collapsed:: true
										- {{video https://youtu.be/r8G7-hQG07o}}
										- Initial state: before enums
										  ```typescript
										  interface Resource<T> { 
										    uid: number; 
										    resourceType: number; 
										    data: T;
										  }
										  
										  const docOne: Resource<object> = { 
										    uid: 1, 
										    resourceType: 3, 
										    data: { title: "name of the wind" }
										  }
										  
										  const docTwo: Resource<object> = { 
										    uid: 180, 
										    resourceType: 4, 
										    data: { name: ‘yoshi’ }
										  }
										  ```
										- Final state: after enums
										  ```typescript
										  enum ResourceType { BOOK, AUTHOR, FILM, DIRECTOR, PERSON }{
										  
										  interface Resource<T> { 
										    uid: number; 
										    resourceType: ResourceType; 
										    data: T;
										  }
										  
										  const docOne: Resource<object> = { 
										    uid: 1, 
										    resourceType: ResourceType.BOOK,
										    data: { title: 'name of the wind' }
										  }
										  
										  const docTwo: Resource<object> = { 
										    uid: 180, 
										    resourceType: ResourceType.PERSON, 
										    data: { name: 'yoshi' }
										  }
										  
										  console.log(docOne, docTwo);
										  ```
							- You don’t need to follow along when watching this tutorial (especially installing TypeScript/anything globally), just try and pick one or two things to takeaway

						- Example
						  ```typescript
						  type FruitBasket = {
						    juicy: string;
						    lotsOf: boolean;
						    colour: string;

						  };
						  ```
					- How to pass down props in TypeScript
						- Example
						  ```tsx
						  type ExampleProps = { 
						    juicy: string; 
						    lotsOf: boolean; 
						    colour: string; 
						    firm: boolean;
						    howManyPips: number;
						  };
						  
						  export default function Example(props: ExampleProps) { 
						    return <p>Just an example</p>;
						  } 
						  
						  <Example 
						  	juicy={"very"} 
						  	lotsOf={true}
						  	colour={"blue"}
						  	firm={true}
						  	howManyPips={5} 
						  />
						  ```
					- React + TS workshop
						- You may find these resources helpful as you work through this workshop:
							- [Minimal TypeScript Crash Course For React - With Interactive Code Exercises](https://profy.dev/article/react-typescript)
							- https://www.carlrippon.com/React-event-handlers-with-typescript/
						- Type vs Interface
							- Interface can be mutated, Type can't
						- Converting a JSX `handleChange`  to TSX
							- ```jsx
							  function onChange(e) { 
							    setTodoTitle(e.target.value);
							  }
							  ```
							- ```tsx
							  function onChange(e:React.ChangeEvent<HTMLInputElement>) { 
							    setTodoTitle(e.target.value);
							  }
							  ```
						- Functions as props in TypeScript
							- Simple checking
							  ```tsx
							  type addFunction = {
							    addTodo: Function
							  }
							  
							  export function AddTodo({addTodo}: addFunction) {
							    // blah
							  }
							  ```
							- Advanced checking:
							  ```typescript
							  type addFunction = {
							    addTodo: (newTitle: string) => void;
							  }
							  
							  export function AddTodo({addTodo}: addFunction) {
							    const { addTodo } = props;
							  }
							  ```
							-
						- In `useState` the first two values are also referred to as setter and getter
						-
					- [`ts-node`](https://typestrong.org/ts-node)
						- transforms TypeScript into JavaScript, enabling you to directly execute TypeScript on Nodes without precompiling
						- [ts-node - npm](https://www.npmjs.com/package/ts-node)
						- Documentation
							- Setup
								- `npm i typescript`
								  Change to globally install TypeScript?
								- `tsc -v` to check TS version
								- `npm i ts-node`
								- `ts-node -v` to check ts-node version
							- Example npm scripts
								- ```json
								  "scripts": {
								      "test": "mocha -r ts-node/register -t 15000 test/**/*.ts",
								      "index": "tsc index.ts",
								      "dev": "tsc --watch",
								      "build": "tsc"
								  }
								  ```
							- `ts-node index.ts` is equivalent to `tsc index.ts && node index.js`
							- Troubleshooting
								- `npm i -d ts-node`
								- `npm i -d typescript`
								- `npm i -d @types/node`

				  id:: bad0d08b-f295-4be9-9789-c335d33a2d90

					- [Learning Resources]
						- Once you've completed the tutorial above and have your app up and running, keep exploring! Ideas include:
							- Customize the todo list app.
							- Research more about GraphQL both by Googling and by exploring the [Amplify GraphQL API docs](https://docs.amplify.aws/lib/graphqlapi/getting-started/q/platform/js/). What are the pros and cons when comparing it to REST? Can you add additional CRUD route requests to the todo list application?
							- You can also use Amplify to create a REST back end. Use the [docs here](https://docs.amplify.aws/lib/restapi/getting-started/q/platform/js/) to try it out.
							- Go deeper into the [Amplify Authentication library](https://docs.amplify.aws/lib/auth/getting-started/q/platform/js/#create-authentication-service) and see if you can customise the auth in your app.
							- Explore other [Amplify libraries](https://docs.amplify.aws/lib/q/platform/js/). What else can you add?
							- Once you feel comfortable with Amplify, you can research and explore
							   other AWS services as well. What are the most commonly used? What would
							   fit with your use case of a full stack app with a React front end, 
							  server, and database if you weren't using Amplify?
						- Other AWS resources:
							- [AWS Cloud Essentials Getting Started Guide](https://aws.amazon.com/getting-started/cloud-essentials/?pg=gs)
							- [FreeCodeCamp article](https://www.freecodecamp.org/news/top-5-things-to-learn-first-when-getting-started-with-aws/)
							- [Full list of AWS services](https://d1.awsstatic.com/whitepapers/aws-overview.pdf)
							- [AWS Certified Cloud Practitioner course](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SOTamWNgDKc)

				- Lily-Lou Lewis from SoC talk about recruitment
				  collapsed:: true
				  id:: 63c581c8-8598-414c-9ab3-0435916fce14
					- Most important thing is CV
						- Most important thing on CV is to get across your personality, and give the reasons why you did certain things in the past
						- Talk briefly about background/past experience
						- Talk about most successful project(s) on bootcamp, with high detail on one
							- Mention challenges overcome
							- Mention various technologies used
						- List your skills normally, don't show a bar chart
						  collapsed:: true
							- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671531447499_0.png)
						- Tell them why you left your previous career
						- Avoid a 1 page CV
						- Hobbies and interests
					- Avoid cover letters unless they're asked for as it's a waste of time
					- Good example of a LinkedIn profile
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671533316154_0.png)
					- #+BEGIN_TIP
					  Post-bootcamp you'll be able to Slack message and call them for several hours at a time to go through your CV for example
					  #+END_TIP
					- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671534182669_0.png)
					- Additional advice from Liz
						- - Make the design of your CV reflect who you are. If you're logical and organised, make your CV neat and formal. If you're artistic and visual, as long as your CV is readable and sane, feel free to get creative with the design.
						- - Make your CV reflect who you are, what you're passionate about, and what you can do. Don't write your CV based on what you think an employer wants to read.
						- - Highlight SoC at the top of your experience (don't bury it in education). This is most important for employers as it shows that you're already doing the doing, working in agile tech teams and delivering. Have a couple of brief lines on what SoC is, and then describe your experience, including a description of your final project with the roles you specifically played in the team and a link to the repo(s). Err to more information about your SoC experience rather than less as this is truly valuable for employers.
						- - However, don't completely chuck out your previous experience!  What you've achieved at School of Code is amazing, but you already have great experience with relevant transferable skills from your career before the bootcamp. Make sure that this is reflected on your CV. Include your previous experience, but don't go into the minutia of details. Just have what you did, when, where, and a point or two about achievements/transferrable skills.
						- - You can also highlight an additional project along with your final project (such as a side project) if you feel like it helps highlight your skills and interest. Make sure to describe what you built and why and have a link to the Github repo.
						- - For your skills, list out names of tech in text, not just symbols (e.g. ensure you include the word React and not just the logo). This will make sure that any automated scanning software picks them up.
						- - Include soft skills in your skills section, but also use where you describe your SoC experience and projects to demonstrate those as well (communication, teamwork, problem solving, etc.).
						- - Your hobbies and interest section is really important - this shows employers who you are, your personality, and your passions. Write two or three sentences about what you like to do, why, and any other context. For example, if you like to run, it could look something like "When I'm not coding, I love to run because X. Recently, I've just run a 10k for Charity XYZ, and I'm planning on training for a half marathon next." This can help employers become interested in you as a person that they'd want to talk to and help differentiate you so you stand out.
						- - Always put that references are available on request. Do not list specific referee details on your CV for GDPR reasons.
						- - Do **not** put your phone number, email, or street address anywhere on your CV. If you do this, because of GDPR we'll have to ask manually if you consent to us sharing your information with each employer instead of just being able to send your CV over as soon as you express interest in a role, and this could cause delays. We'd hate to see you miss an opportunity because of something like this!
						- - Do include links to your Github profile and your LinkedIn profile! These are publicly available info and don't have any GDPR concerns.
						- - Make your CV as a PDF as this is universal - no matter what software an employer is using, they'll be able to open a PDF.
						- - Include clickable links, but ensure that they'll work long-term. For example, for a project, include the link to the Github repo rather than the deployed link (the current deployed link should be in the readme anyway). You could change hosting/URL/etc. or do something down the line that could possibly break the link, whereas the repo link will stay the same.

				- SoC LinkedIn training
				  collapsed:: true
					- {:height 589, :width 1217}
					- What is LinkedIn Recruiter?
						- LinkedIn recruiter is a premium tool offered by LinkedIn, that allows recruiters & talent teams to help them find the right candidate. Recruiter lets you filter through every LinkedIn profile by location, work experience, job title, company size, skill set.
					- Why does this matter to you?
						- Understanding the mechanisms of LinkedIn Recruiter will help you become more visible to people, EG you could be a perfect fit for a position, but if your LinkedIn profile is not optimised you will never be found.
						- Optimising your LinkedIn in terms of keywords, skills, description - increases your visibility, increasing your opportunities to hearing about new roles.
					- Recruiters spend hours on LinkedIn everyday - searching for the right candidate. Literally hours.
					- Hiring Managers also use LinkedIn to look for candidates, typically via a job ad. More often than not, ona LinkedIn job ad, the hiring manager is going to look at your LinkedIn profile before they look at your CV.
					- Case study
					  collapsed:: true
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671629656139_0.png)
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671629663484_0.png)
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671629716444_0.png)
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671629744623_0.png)
					- ![image.png](../assets/image_1671629777067_0.png)
						- Endorse people you've worked with
					- Creating and sharing content on LinkedIn is essential to get the most out of the platform. Every piece of quality content you share makes you more visible to hiring managers, recruiters, and industry leaders.
						- LinkedIn content has its roots in long form articles, but today, short form posts and video are encouraged and promoted. Short form posts are an easy way to get started, as you can use them to comment on and share third-party content.
						- Content posted on LinkedIn should provide value to other users. Consider thinking of other LinkedIn users as subscribers, and try to provide content that is relevant to the audience you want to reach.
						- #+BEGIN_TIP
						  Write blog posts as well as short-form content
						  #+END_TIP

			- Week 13: final project week 1
			  collapsed:: true
				- Day 1
					- Teams: [Notion – The all-in-one workspace for your notes, tasks, wikis, and databases.](https://schoolofcode.notion.site/BC13-Final-Project-Teams-2b97f2b2963c4fe384261806c29da708)
					- **Project Rhythm:**
					  collapsed:: true
						- Daily
						  collapsed:: true
							- Standups
							- Standup within your team - 9:10-9:30
							- One person (different person each day) joins the “standup of standups” at 9:30 across the teams in the ABC groups with a coach to share priorities, blockers, and questions for the day.
							- Retros
							- At the end of each day (around 16:25), retro within your team.
							- When we close the day at 16:50, randomly selected teams will summarise their retro for the whole cohort; nominate who will speak so you’re prepared if your team is chosen.
						- Wednesdays - coach check ins
						  collapsed:: true
							- Coaches visiting individual teams to talk through progress and any blockers and check in around milestones
							- Be prepared to talk through where you’re at with your project
						- Fridays of week 1 and week 3 - show and tells
						  collapsed:: true
							- Gathering in ABC rooms starting approx. 4pm on Friday, similar to hackathon presentations
							- 5 min per team
							- Show and talk through what you’ve accomplished that week, progress you’ve made, any blockers, and key learnings
						- Friday of week 2 - demo afternoon
						  collapsed:: true
							- Full formal demos (approx. 15 min with 5 min for feedback/questions at the end)
							- Split into two groups of ten teams rather than ABC groups
							- More guidance to be shared shortly

						- Mentee currently is Julio Camargo
						- His story
						  collapsed:: true
							- He wasted years doing odd jobs up to 25, then decided he wanted to be a programmer
							- Did a 1 year course part-time, already had a full-time job. Borrowed a computer and used a floppy disk
							- Paid about £2.5k in 1994 (he's 53 in 2022)
							- 1 year as a salesman in a computer shop. Played with Windows 95 a lot in quiet hours

							- Know where to find answers (e.g. Stack Overflow)
							- You'll all suffer Imposter Syndrome at some point. It's a natural feeling that "you're going to get found out as being not good enough"

					  collapsed:: true
						- Teamwork + Collaboration + About Me
						- Use "I", not "we". Big contrast to what Nadeem said
							- He as an employer wants to know what you specifically contributed to
							- If he hears "we", he thinks "not you", that somebody else said it
							- Don't say "we" 0%,
						- Enthusiasm whilst talking is very important

						- [Home | BAE Systems | United Kingdom](https://www.baesystems.com/en-uk/home)
							- [BAE Systems - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems)
								- **BAE Systems plc** (**BAE**) is a British [multinational](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multinational_corporation) [arms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arms_industry), [security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_security), and [aerospace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerospace) company based in [London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London), England.[7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-7)[8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-8) It is the largest defence contractor in [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe),[9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-9) and ranked the seventh-largest in the world based on applicable 2021 revenues.[10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-10) As of 2017, it is the biggest manufacturer in Britain.[11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-veconomist-11) Its largest operations are in the United Kingdom and United States, where its [BAE Systems Inc.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems_Inc.) subsidiary is one of the six largest suppliers to the [US Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense). Other major markets include Australia, Canada, Japan, India, Saudi Arabia, Turkey, Qatar, Oman and Sweden, where Saudi Arabia is regularly among its top three sources of revenue.[12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-12)[11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-veconomist-11)[13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-13)[14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Systems#cite_note-14)
						- National Security Engineering Lead

						- Big company benefits, Small company atmosphere
							- Our culture is underpinned by an environment where it’s okay to:
								- Talk to the “boss”
								- Dress appropriately for the situation (our people
								- Have an opinion that's different from others — but express it with respect
								- wear everything from suits to jeans and t-shirts
								- Call out non-inclusive behaviour
								- Suggest improvements
								- Work smart (and go home)
								- Work flexible hours
								- Fail, and learn from mistakes
								- Go on holiday - and not check your emails!
								- Ask for help
								- Laugh
								- Celebrate success
						- The types of work you will be doing
							- We generally work in project teams using modern Agile and DevOps methodologies
							- We develop software systems to solve our customers’ mission critical problems
							- Often we help our customers make sense of large amounts of data and information
							- We use the latest technologies, for example AWS, Azure, Al and Machine Learning
							- There is huge variety in the work we do
						- Your career
							- The opportunities are there — we will help you build a rewarding career
							- Think of your career as navigating a climbing wall - you are always progressing, but sometimes you need to take side steps to get to a better position
							- Your career can go in all different directions
								- Expert senior Software Engineer
								- Technical Team Lead
								- Data engineering specialist
								- Scrum master
							- You will work with your dedicated career manager to build a career which suits you
						- The work we do is meaningful: a child protection case study (Operation Notarise)
						  id:: 63f33e8d-9917-43bb-8671-fca5ee9b4e04
							- BAE systems helped our customer, the CEOP* unit, to dismantle a major paedophile ring
							- CEOP = Child Exploitation and Online Protection
							- “In Operation Notarise — an unprecedented six- month operation coordinated by the NCA— our BAE team developed bespoke automation tools that saved CEOP an estimated 10 years of effort. Without this support we could not have carried out the operation in the way we did and achieve such widespread results. Notarise led to the safeguarding of over 400 children across the UK and the arrest of over 660 suspected paedophiles.”
							- Johnny Gwynne, Director, National Crime Agency CEOP Command talking about our BAE Systems National Security team.
						- Why we need people like you
							- * There is an ever growing demand for BAE system to help our customers respond to these challenges ...
							  * They come to us for skilled engineering teams who can design, build and run capabilities which help to make the UK safer
							  * Our customers particular value the quality of our junior engineers
							  * And that’s where you come in!
						- What we offer
							- £30k+ per annum starting salary
							- A modern benefits package which allows you to select options which meet your needs
							- A dedicated BAE Systems Career Manager to support you as your career develops
							- Continued learning and development throughout your career
							- 25 days paid annual leave (5 days per year can be purchased or sold)
							- Sponsorship to achieve the highest levels of security clearance in UK
							- The opportunity to build a career using the latest tech in a domain where what you do can have a real world impact on the security of the UK
						- Where is the work?
							- 2-3 days each hybrid
							- On joining, you will be based in one of our BAE Systems offices — Leeds, Manchester, Gloucester or London
							- We have embraced hybrid working which means your work will normally be a mix of working at home and in an office
							- However when you get higher clearance you will be expected to spend the majority of your week in an office or client site
							- Travel — whilst much of our work is centred around these locations you may be asked to travel and work across UK as the business
							  need arises
						- Who we are looking for
							- ![image.png](../assets/image_1674129264381_0.png)

								- If you stayed in some countries for 6 months+ it can be an issue. Have a conversation with us about it
						- Tips from a SoC graduate working there
							- Ask questions constantly, it's beneficial to everyone
							- They became a tech lead for a temporary project because they knew React whereas the rest of the team were backend devs

			- [[Feb 6th, 2023]] alter-egos, and interview question prep
			  collapsed:: true
				- Alter-egos - channel a different one to gain psychological distance, and emulate their traits
					- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675676249082_0.png)
					- What
					- Who
					- Why
					- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675676332580_0.png)
					- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675676350128_0.png)
				- d
					- If you work with a startup, ask them
						- By what date do you predict you'll be profitable?
						- How much runway do you have? i.e. until what date
				- [Employability Kumspace](https://www.kumospace.com/employability-)
					- Remember to read through the star method together before you get started: [How To Use the STAR Interview Response Technique | Indeed.com](https://www.indeed.com/career-advice/interviewing/how-to-use-the-star-interview-response-technique)
					- Here’s a list of interview questions for you to practice in your groups. Take turns answering a different question, one each - then give time for feedback from the rest of the group once finished.
						- • Give me an example of a time when you had a difference of opinion with a team member. How did you handle that?
						  • What was the most difficult part/learning curve about the school of code?
						  • Tell me about a time your work responsibilities got a little overwhelming. What did you do?
						  • Give an example of when your communication skills helped benefit a team.
						  • What experience could you bring from your previous jobs to benefit the tech industry?
					- Here’s what you should be looking for when your team-mate is answering an interview question. Make notes and give them feedback once they’ve finished.
						- Did the candidate pick a relevant example?
						  Did they give a clear overview of the situation, explain what the situation was and how they handled it?
						  Did they show enthusiasm/enjoy the challenge of the question?
						  Did they take ownership/show humility by not blaming others in the situation? (Where applicable)
						  Did they show growth? (Where applicable)
						  Did they show good teamwork? (Where applicable)
						  Did they show self-awareness? (Where applicable)
			- [[Feb 8th, 2023]] Tom Pauley tips mostly
			  collapsed:: true
				- Getting Things Done (GTD)
					- Your mind is for having ideas, not holding them
					- Steps
						- 1) Capture
						- 2) Clarify
						  collapsed:: true
							- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675849023180_0.png)
						- 3) Organise
						  collapsed:: true
							- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675849073224_0.png)
						- 4) Engage
				- Tom Pauley tips
					- Build a network
						- Go to a couple meetups a month, digital-only is fine
							- Go to talks + the social meetups after
							- Also make friends with the organisers
					- CV
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675849942641_0.png)
						- Don't talk in 3rd-person
						- Don't just list logos of things you've used - link it to projects or work experiences
						- Show a journal of your learning both pre- and post-bootcamp
					- Before applications/interviews
					  id:: 63e371b8-66de-4daf-b6b7-d03901fe6093
						- **Know yourself**. Have 2 - 3 min intro pitch ready. Who you are, what you care about, what you've done. Where you want to be.
						- **Upsell**. Don’t down play other experience. Second career humans and life outside work matters. Moving into tech doesn’t mean youre back to step 1.
						- **Research (company)**. Website, Google, News, Techcrunch, Twitter. Understand what they do, Understand the who the customer iS.
						- **Research (interviewers)**. If you know the names of the interviewers have a look at them on LinkedIn.
						- **Know the process.** What are the stages. How long is each stage. How many interviewers. What is the stage designed to test.
						- **Have questions.** What are they working on? How do the teams work? Why are they hiring for this position? What support do they offer to help you progress?
						- **Practice, practice**
					- During interview
						- Some signals
							- Be thankful + kind
								- Say - thanks for the opportunity, ask how their week is going. Show interestin their work.
							- Listen + take notes
								- Say - | hope you don’t mind but I'd like to take notes. Play back things they say as you go.
							- Open by default
								- Say - | know | don’t have all the skills you’re asking for but | learn fast and | want to prove I’m worth the risk.
							- Want the job
								- Not many people really do their research. Show that you know about the company and you’re excited to work with them.
							- Fail gracefully
								- If you don’t know or get something wrong. Be honest, ask questions, take notes.
							- Be growing
								- Show that you’re engaged, motivated and have a plan.Talk about your learning plan.
						- Interviewers are looking for
							- Values and Behaviours
								- Honest, transparent and open
								- Engaged, passionate and excited
								- Growth mindset
								- Agency, Autonomy and Ownership
							- e.g. telling them about a time when you failed
							-
					- Technical tests
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675850679640_0.png)
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675850806536_0.png)
					- Summary
					  collapsed:: true
						- ![image.png](../assets/image_1675851061047_0.png)

						- e.g. [JSMonthly Feb Meetup , Thu, Feb 23, 2023, 7:00 PM   | Meetup](https://www.meetup.com/js-monthly/events/291133574/)
					- Other tips
						- Keep list of your skills small because it takes up lots of space above the fold

			  collapsed:: true
				- Ikigai - japanese word
					- ![image.png](../assets/image_1676281137399_0.png)
				- Hamza on tech tests
					- From a real tech test
						- ### Questions
						  collapsed:: true
							- `~/Documents/Git/1MY REPOS/Assorted/tech-test-aaron-and-fabbiha`
							- 1) Comparing the app-original and app-standalone code bases (functional class components vs hooks). The app-standalone code base has put each component in a separate file and directory structure.
							  Why do you think that was done, what are the advantages / disadvantages?
								- Pros
									- Separation of concerns
									- Readability / quicker onboarding
									- Debugging easier + less bugs
								- Cons
									- Can be confusing how everything interacts with each other
										- Visual component tree may become necessary
									- Prematurely optimising can cause issues with trying new features
									- Can take time to learn and adjust to new paradigm, causing bugs/costing money/time to learn/loss of expertise
									- More complicated to plan out
							- 2) Thinking about a production ready app, what do you think is missing from all the examples? Hint: the square component in the standalone app has one
								- Types
								- Tests
								- Error handling (e.g. try...catch)
							- 3) Are you familiar with Redux? If so what is the basic idea behind it and what would be a good case for using it?
								- ((6396f61d-f951-4ca8-baf8-ba8937b02e1d))
							- 4) If you are interested in the full-stack role Please take a look at the partial implementation of an express routes in backend/router.js.
							  id:: 63ea1938-5a8e-4b77-a3d5-4a72dc88ba02
							  Thinking of a production application, what issues do you see with this code? List as many as you like
								- There's no `package.json`
								- No unit tests
								- No types
								- No initialisation of Express app
								- No error handling (e.g. `try...catch`)
								- No models or routes - modularity is important for separation of concerns
								- No port specified for Express app
								-
								- ^^Use this mongoDB template in the future^^

					- ABOUT THE COMPANY:
						- OAG is a leading global travel data provider, that has been powering the growth and innovation of the air travel ecosystem since 1929. Every day, we support millions of journeys across the globe, enabling a simpler, seamless and more enjoyable travel experience. With the world’s largest network of schedules and status data, and leading-edge analytics tools, we enable our customers to make smarter decisions, better adapt to change, and create exceptional customer experiences. We partner with some of the biggest global brands, airports, airlines, travel operators, and fast-growing start-ups to design the best services available today, and the finest innovations of tomorrow. Now we are looking for Software Engineers to join the team in Luton.
					- YOU WILL BE RESPONSIBLE FOR:
						- Applying technical skills to help the business achieve its goals
						- Contributing to product development related activities
						- Applying Agile principals effectively in day-to-day activities
						- Participating in story sizing and breakdown
						- Writing clean and maintainable code
						- Producing well-structured documentation
						- Sharing business domain and technical knowledge across the team
						- Keeping up to date with relevant technologies and best practices
					- IF YOU HAVE:
						- An interest or experience in Java with a focus on Backend Service Engineering
						- An interest or experience in relational database technologies
						- An interest or experience in Continuous Delivery (CI/CD) Practices
						- An interest or experience in applying Agile methodologies (any of these: Scrum, Kanban, DSDM)
						- An interest or experience in using Unit testing frameworks
						- Great communication skills and willing to work in a team
						- Sense of ownership and pride in your performance and its impact on company’s success
					- WE WILL OFFER YOU:
						- Work with people who are passionate about technology and business domain
						- Opportunity to travel to our other offices
						- Ability to join an industry leading international company
						- Attractive compensation and benefits package
						- Great growth and development opportunities
						- Supported training in areas that you need to succeed
					- **The 2 hour interview will have the following structure:**
						- 60 mins talking through personality, drive and technical/work experience questions
						- 30 mins logic problem (thinking time) – candidate will work with the Teams session switched on, but work in pseudocode or javascript (or any preferred structured language)
						- 20 mins walkthrough solution and Q&A with candidate – note we are not looking for a perfect solution but insights into how the candidate tackles problems
						- 10 mins candidate questions

				- Vetting (security clearance)
					- [United Kingdom Security Vetting: Applicant - GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/guidance/united-kingdom-security-vetting-applicant#levels-of-national-security-clearance)
					  collapsed:: true
						- ### Interview format
							- A routine eSC, DV or eDV interview will cover all aspects of your life. At the interview, the 
							  vetting officer will build as complete a picture of you as possible. The
							   purpose of this is so we can make an informed assessment that you will 
							  be able to cope with access to sensitive information or assets at the 
							  highest levels and will not become a security risk and a threat to 
							  national security.
							- Key themes include:
								- your loyalty, honesty and reliability, and identifying any vulnerabilities that could lead you to being bribed or blackmailed
								- your wider family background (relationships and influences)
								- past experiences of drug taking (if any)
								- financial affairs
								- general political views
								- foreign travel
								- hobbies.
							- If you are asked to attend an interview in relation to a CTC, Level 1B or SC application, the interview will usually cover a specific area of your life, but may extend to include questions asked in a full DV interview.
					- How to approach the interview
						- Be completely honest.
						- The interview will be very searching, but it is not an interrogation and should not feel like one. Some of the questions will be intrusive but are asked because we are trying to find out if you are vulnerable to pressure.
						- Sometimes people have aspects of their lives that they are ashamed or embarrassed to tell us about. Usually these are of little or no security significance. They will generally not stop or restrict the granting of a security clearance.
						- The Vetting Officer will be open-minded and is not there to make moral judgements on people’s lifestyles. They will only be interested in assessing potential security risks. It is essential therefore that you are open and honest at all stages of the interview process.
						- If you have any doubts about the relevance of some questions you should ask the vetting officer why they are asking the question.
						- We will probably refuse your clearance, or subsequently withdraw it, if we later find out that you have lied or withheld information.

				  collapsed:: true
					- Junior Software Engineer at Percayso
					- ## Percayso
					  
					  **We’re an innovative InsureTech company led and backed by a successful technology entrepreneur and venture capital.**
					  
					  We
					   provide highly scalable real-time data enrichment APIs that deliver 
					  critical data-based insights to insurers at the point of quote. Our APIs
					   handle millions of transactions a day and we are looking to expand the 
					  breadth and depth of our product offering.
					  
					  Alongside **flexible and remote working** we offer a fun, friendly working environment, **Pension**, **Health Insurance **and **free share options** in the company for all employees.
					- ## You
					  
					  **You’re a budding technologist looking to learn while getting stuff done.**
					  
					  You’re
					   starting out in your technology career. You’re curious, 
					  self-disciplined and thrive working as part of a small cohesive team. 
					  You’re a proactive, positive, can-do kind of person, looking to grow and
					   develop your skills.
					- ## The role
					  
					  This
					   is a remote-first role. However, occasional travel to the head office 
					  in Nottingham or other meeting locations may be required.
					  
					  You
					   will be joining a small team of highly capable engineers building our 
					  core product suite capable of processing millions of transactions daily.
					  
					  You’ll
					   build our solutions in a sustainable way and to modern standards and 
					  share your knowledge to help others to do the same. You will have the 
					  ability to pick up new concepts quickly, and an opportunity to broaden 
					  your skills across the wider technology stack we use; learning from our 
					  other experienced engineers.
					- ### **The role will typically involve**
					- Platform development using our core technologies
					- Sharing knowledge with other team members
					- Building new features and supporting others to do the same
					- Improving our development practices
					- Testing and test automation
					- Building & managing infrastructure and services
					- Planning and estimating technical work
					- Automating manual repetitive tasks
					- Anything else that might reasonably be required to help us ship, manage and maintain great software!
					- ### **Core technologies**
					  
					  For
					   this role, and at this level, you only need JavaScript or TypeScript 
					  coding skills. Everything else is beneficial, but not required.
					- ((629ccb26-3115-4d41-b4db-a686fe51a4a2))
					- Javascript/Typescript
					- ((6457bcad-7919-46a4-a9c0-8bb0ddf40189))
					- AWS Fargate
					- ((64b7c5ea-fc23-4c8f-bba3-40309679cf7d))
					- ElasticSearch
					- ((6463499e-dc33-4af7-bbb7-33338a8a325b))
					- AWS DynamoDB
					- AWS Elasticache
					- ### **Secondary technologies**
					  
					  For this role, and at this level, having experience with any of these practices would be beneficial
					- Docker
					- Python
					- Sparkling Logic
					- ((63bae0ae-2db2-4cf2-b923-755efe250d86))
					- Nextcloud
					- Hubspot
					- PHP
					- MySQL
					- ### **Software development practices**
					  
					  For this role, and at this level, having experience with any of these technologies would be beneficial
					- Git source control
					- Scrum
					- Pair programming
					- Test Driven Development (TDD)
					- Testing (Unit, Integration, Functional or Load)
					- Application Security
					- Software delivery pipelines (CI/CD)
					- Automation
